QUESADA LADERO, Miguel Ángel

1. PERSONAL DATA



Name: Miguel Angel

Surname: Ladero Quesada

D.N.I.: 12.139.097 L



Birth date: January 14, 1943

Birthplace: Valladolid

Address: C/ Minister Ibáñez Martín 3, 2nd (Madrid)

C.P.: 28015

Tfo.: 91/544.37.43





Current professional status



Organism: Complutense University of Madrid

Center: Faculty of Geography and History

Department: Medieval History Department

Category: University Professor since 22.X.1971. Retired on 30.ix.2013

UNESCO CODES: 550403, 550302, 550301

NAB codes: 0.800, 0.860, 0.870







Academic training



Bachelor: Philosophy and Letters (History)



Center: University of Valladolid

Date: June 1,964. Title, October 22, 1964

Qualification: Outstanding, Extraordinary Prize





Doctorate: History



Center: University of Valladolid

Date: June 1.967. Title, July 27, 1967

Qualification: Outstanding Cum Laude, Extraordinary Prize

Thesis Director: Professor Don Luis Suárez Fernández





















Professional scientific activities





I. Posts occupied in universities





A) Teaching/research



1. Professor Numerary of History of the Middle Ages at the Faculty of Geography and History of the Complutense University (Madrid) from January 1978 to September 2013. Full time.



2. Professor Numerary of History of the Universal Middle Ages and Spain of the University of Seville from March 1974 to January 1978. Full time.



3. Professor Numerary of History of the Universal Middle Ages and Spain of the University of La Laguna (Canary Islands), from October 1971 to March 1974. Full time.



4. Added Professor of History of the Universal Middle Ages and Spain of the Complutense University, appointed in October 1971 (did not take possession).



5. Added Professor of History of the Universal Middle Ages and Spain at the University of La Laguna from May 1970 to October 1971. Full time.



6. Professor for opposition of universal history at the Faculty of Philosophy and Letters of the Complutense University from April 1969 to May 1970. Part -time.

3. Doctor “Honoris Causa” from the University of Huelva. Appointed by agreement of the Cloister of the University of July 17, 2015.



5. Honorary Member of the Institute of Medieval and Renaissance Studies of the University of La Laguna de Tenerife (rectoral appointment of March 4, 2015).

5. Honorary Professor of the Complutense University of Madrid during the 2014-2015 academic courses, 2015-2016















II. Files



1. of the Auxiliary Corps of Archives, Libraries and Museums from May 1961 to July 1966, destined in the General Archive of Simancas.



2. Of the optional body of archivists, librarians and archaeologists from July 1966 to May 1970, destined in the Ministries of Finance (Central Archive) and Presidency of the Government (Technical General Secretariat).











III. Superior Council of Scientific Investigations



1. Scholar of the “Jerónimo Zurita” History Institute in 1967.



2. Contract collaborator between 1968 and 1973.



3. Doctor linked from May 1979 to the extinction of the Institute in January 1985.











IV. Secondary education



1. GEOGRAPHY AND HISTORY PROFESSOR AND TECHNICAL DIRECTOR OF THE RECOGNIZED CENTER OF BACHILLERAO ELEMENTAL COLLEGE CASTILLA, DE VALLADOLID, IN THE COURSE 1964-1965.





























Participation in R&D projects financed in public calls





1.- Principal Researcher of the 4277/79 Plan of the Commission for Scientific and Technical Research, on “Studies on Spanish Society in the Low Middle Ages: Corona de Castilla. XIV and seventeenth centuries. ”



2.- Principal researcher of the PR 84-0309 Plan of CICYT on “Society and power in the low Hispanic Middle Ages. CORONA DE CASTILLA, 1252-1516 ”.



3.- Principal researcher of the PS 90-0050 Plan of DGICYT, Sectorial Program for the General Promotion of Knowledge on “Power, Society and Culture in the Crown of Castile (XIV-XV centuries)”.



4.- Principal Researcher of the PB98-0807 Plan of the General Promotion Promotion Program of the Ministry of Education and Culture, on “The accounts of the Castilian monarchy. 1454-1516 ”. For the 2000-2002 triennium.



5.- Principal researcher of the Special APC1999- 0189 of the General Promotion Promotion Program of the Ministry of Education and Culture, on “Enrique IV of Castile and its time (1445-1474). Documentation of the Royal Academy of History and the General Archive of Simancas ”. Year 2000.

Continued in the special action BHA-2001-4692-E, year 2002, with the same title.



6. Principal researcher of the Special Action BHA-2001-4693-E, developed during 2002 on the theme “Lugient of faith against the Alcorán de Juan Martín de Figuerola. Study and editing ”.



7.Principal researcher of the BHA-2002-03292 research project (Ministry of Science and Technology), on the topic “Real Finance, Political Power and Society in Castilla (1406-1474-1516)”. For the 2003-2005 triennium.



8. Main researcher of the HUM2006-0534/HIST research project, “Research on Castile in the fifteenth century: society, economy and political power”. For the Triennium October 2006-September 2009.



9. Responsible, together with Prof. Dr. José Manuel Nieto Soria, of the consolidated research group of the Complutense University No. 930369, “Society, power and culture in the Crown of Castile. XIII-XVI centuries ”. Subsidized in 2006. It is still valid.

Outstanding cum laude.



14. The manors of the Order of Santiago in his "Province of León" during the fifteenth century. Daniel Rodriguez Blanco. University of Seville, September 1983. (published by the Provincial Council of Badajoz). Outstanding cum laude.



15. Medieval History of Plasencia and its Geo-Historic environment: the Sierra de Béjar and the Sierra de Gredos. Elisa Carolina de Santos Canalejo. Complutense University, Madrid, June 1984. (Published by the Provincial Council of Cáceres). Outstanding cum laude.



16. The Monacato and the Dominos del Cister in Castilla y León. XII to XV centuries. Javier Pérez-Embid Wamba. Complutense University, Madrid, December 1984. (Published by the Junta de Castilla y León). Outstanding cum laude.



17. The small urban nobility of Seville and Jerez de la Frontera during the low Middle Ages. Rafael Sánchez Sous. Complutense University, Madrid, May 1986. (Published by the University of Cádiz and the Provincial Council of Seville). Outstanding cum laude.



18. The Cabildo Cathedral of Segovia and its domain: a model for the agrarian evolution of Castilla in the Low Middle Ages. Miguel Santamaría Lancho. Complutense University, Madrid, June 1986. Outstanding Cum Laude.



19. Ubeda and Baeza in the low Middle Ages. María Josefa Parejo Delgado. Complutense University, Madrid, June 1986. (Published complete in microfiche and partially by Ed. Don Quixote, Sevilla). Apt cum laude unanimously. Exrtraordinary Prize.



20. Jerez de la Frontera in the low Middle Ages. Antonio González Gómez. University of Seville, July 1988. Apt Cum Laude unanimously.



21. The Church of Córdoba in the Low Middle Ages. Illuminated Sanz Sancho. Complutense University, Madrid, October 1988. (Published by the Complutense University of Madrid. And in magazine articles. By the Areces Foundation in 2007). Apt cum laude unanimously.



22. The four villas of the Costa de la Mar de Castilla la Vieja or Low Mountain of Burgos in the Low Middle Ages. Miguel Angel Suárez Garmendia. University of Seville, December 1988. Apt Cum Laude Unanimity.



23. The Judeoconverses at the time and in the court of the Catholic Monarchs. María Rábade Obradó. Complutense University, Madrid, February 1990. (Published by the Complutense University of Madrid. Partially Ed. Sigillum, Madrid, and magazine articles). Apt cum laude unanimously.



24. Soria and its "land" in the low Middle Ages. Maximum Diago Hernando. Complutense University, Madrid, April 1990. (Published by the Complutense University and by the Junta de Castilla y León, partially). Apt cum laude unanimously.



25. Trujillo and his "land" in the low Middle Ages. María del Carmen Fernández-Daza Alvear. Complutense University, Madrid, September 1990. (published bythe Board of Extremadura). Apt cum laude unanimously.



26. Los Téllez-Girón, Condes de Urueña, and the origins of the House of Osuna (1440-1525). Francisco Javier Aguado González. Complutense University, Madrid, October 1990. (Published by the Complutense University). Apt cum laude unanimously.



27. The economic life of the stone monastery in the first half of the fourteenth century. María de la Concepción de la Fuente Cobos. Complutense University. Complutense University, Madrid. December 1991. Apt cum laude unanimously. (Published by the Complutense University and by the Fernando Institution the Catholic of the Diputación de Zaragoza).



28. The monastery of Santa Clara la Real de Toledo. 1360-1797. María Luisa Pérez de Tudela and Bueso. Complutense University, Madrid. July 1993. Apt cum laude unanimously.



29. The Toledo Cathedral and culture in the Middle Ages. Books and libraries. Ramón Gonzálvez Ruiz. May 19, 1994. Complutense University, Madrid. Apt cum laude unanimously

(Publ. Ramón Areces Foundation. Monumenta Toletanae Ecclesiae Historical)



30. Los Manrique: noble lineage, society and politics in the low Castilian Middle Ages. Rosa Montero Tejada. June 20, 1994. National University of Distance Education. Apt cum laude unanimously. (Publ. Savings and Mount of Madrid Box).



31. The Infantado House (1350-1531). Political relations, stately power and lineage organization. Ana Belén Sánchez Prieto. Complutense University, Madrid, July 8, 1994. Apt Cum Laude Unanimity. (Publ. The Burgundy Persevening. Madrid, 2000)



32. Jewish communities in the bishopric of Sigüenza in the low Middle Ages: transformation and disintegration of Judaism in Castile in the late Middle Ages. Javier Castaño González. September 20, 1994. Complutense University, Madrid. Apt cum laude unanimously.



33. The female convents of Toledo. XII to XVI centuries. Laura Canabal Rodríguez. June 1997. Complutense University, Madrid. Apt Cum Laude.



34. The last decade of Isabel la Católica through the General Treasury of Alonso de Morales (1495-1505). Andrés Díaz Rosana. December 1998. Complutense University, Madrid. Outstanding cum laude. (Publ. University Institute "Simancas" of the University of Valladolid).



35. The ideals of the Bajomedieval mission in the conquest of America. Luis Anselmo Duarte Duarte. January 1999. Complutense University, Madrid. Outstanding. (Publ. Spanish University Foundation, Madrid, 2001).



36. THE CARTUJA ORDER IN CASTILLA. 1390-1561. Santiago Cantera Montenegro. 18 May 2000. Complutense University, Madrid. Outstanding cum laude. (Publ. Analecta Cartusiana, Salzburg, 2001).



37. The Cabildo of the Toledo Cathedral in the fifteenth century. Institutional and sociological aspects. María José Lop Otín. Complutense University, Madrid. February 8, 2002. Outstanding Cum Laude. 22. The Church of Cartagena in the fourteenth century. Illuminated Sanz Sancho. Complutense University. February 1982. (Publ. In medieval Spain).

24. Calatayud's customs in the mid -fifteenth century. María del Carmen García Herrero. Complutense University. September 1982. (Publ. In medieval Spain).



25. The Court of the Catholic Monarchs in Gonzalo Fernández de Oviedo. Margarita Rey Varona. Complutense University. September 1982.

27. oGranada edges in the first half of the sixteenth century. María Teresa de Diego Velasco. Complutense University. February 1983. (Publ. In medieval Spain).



28. Fiscal nomenclators of the Crown of Castile in the fifteenth century. Francisco Javier Aguado González. Complutense University. September 1983.



29. Ordinances of Hita and La Puebla de Alcocer. Luis Miguel de la Cruz Herranz. Complutense University. June 1984. (Publ. In medieval Spain).



30. Ordinances of Colmenar Viejo, Méntrida and San Martín de Valdeiglesias. Adrián Arcaz del Pozo. Complutense University. September 1984.

33. Alfonso XI and Seville: The real systems. María Teresa Bueno Oliveros. Complutense University. March 1985.



34. Manzanares el Real and his county through the ordinances of the fifteenth and sixteenth centuries. María del Pilar Díaz Asensio. Complutense University. April 1985.



35. The taxation of the crown in the kingdom of Galicia. 1475-1516. Rocío Pizarro Jurado. Complutense University. September 1985.



36. Brotherhoods and hospitals in the Caja Calatrava at the end of the fifteenth century. Raquel Torres Jiménez. Complutense University. September 1985. (Publ. Ciudad Real).



37. Salamanca in the fifteenth century. Isabel Alvargonzález Jorissen. Complutense University. September 1985.



38. The city and commerce of La Coruña. XII to XV centuries. María Luisa Albor Moreno. Complutense University. October 1985.



[The Faculty of Geography and History of the Complutense University suppressed the reading of bachelor's memoirs in June 1986. The following titles correspond to work of the doctoral program of the Medieval History Department, of characteristics equivalent to the memoirs]



39. The manor of Capilla. XV century. María José Lop Otín. Complutense University. 1987-1988 course. (Publ. In medieval Spain).

Santiago González Sánchez. Complutense University. March 1999.

Participation in international committees and representations



1. Spanish Committee of Historical Sciences (Member of the International Committee of Historical Sciences):

Treasurer since April 1981.

Vice President since March 1993.

President since 2013.

Member of its Board of Directors since June 1983, Vice President for the Sexenio 1989-1995. Re-elected for 1995-2001. Member of the Board of Directors from May 2001. Vice President from May 2005 to June 2007.
